You can see the Northern Lights – also called Aurora Borealis – in many places, from the northern parts of Norway, Sweden, Greenland, Iceland, Finland to the northwest of Russia, most of Alaska and northern parts of Canada. And for those ticking off the Southern Lights – or Aurora Australis – too, head to the southernmost parts of Argentina, South Georgia Island, southern Tasmania in Australia, Stewart Island in New Zealand or for those who really favour the cold, Antarctica. 📸 @gabriel.desanti\n\n#LiveCurious #NorthernLights #AuroraBorealis #SouthernLights #AuroraAustralis #LiveCurious #BucketList #Nature #Adventure #NightSky

bookingcom;https://scontent-dus1-1.cdninstagram.com/v/t51.2885-15/e35/s1080x1080/72781807_940880356288316_217038799524680177_n.jpg?_nc_ht=scontent-dus1-1.cdninstagram.com&_nc_cat=108&_nc_ohc=3OZjUZKdXf8AX94gMDH&oh=ac5cf075ea7ff1293eeff043b9223807&oe=5E951CB8;69;3201;Salins d’Aigues Mortes is a coastal town in the South of France where you’ll discover a number of piercingly bright pink salt marshes. bookingcom;https://scontent-dus1-1.cdninstagram.com/v/t51.2885-15/e35/16906941_253286188453318_3531200898204172288_n.jpg?_nc_ht=scontent-dus1-1.cdninstagram.com&_nc_cat=110&_nc_ohc=hmSLk_107MAAX_LWzyy&oh=7339c819f711590e047ac02bf91beb31&oe=5E92889A;25;2172;Plitvička Jezera is a National Park in the centre of Croatia. With a chain of 16 terraced lakes joined by cascading waterfalls, it’s the perfect place to take a walk.
